<div id="review_2346580347" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2346580347" />
    <a title="Dana Ilie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21690081-dana-ilie"><img alt="Dana Ilie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1584606424p2/21690081.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2346580347?book_show_action=true">Dec 18, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dana Ilie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dana Ilie" href="/user/show/21690081-dana-ilie">Dana Ilie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Dana by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/31562637-simona-vlad">Simona Vlad</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21690081-dana-ilie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2346580347" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7660585558577680883">Why has it taken me this long to read Robin Hobb? Truthfully, I am not quite sure. Fears aside, I took the plunge, and can assuredly say it was well worth the wait!<br/>For the sake of clarity, I started with the first of the various series which make up the books set within the Realm of the Elderlings. This meant starting with Assassins Apprentice, the first installment in the Farseer Trilogy. <br/>I have really fallen in love with Robin Hobb’s style of writing. It has so much substance and sophisticatio</span>
  <span id="freeText7660585558577680883" style="display:none">Why has it taken me this long to read Robin Hobb? Truthfully, I am not quite sure. Fears aside, I took the plunge, and can assuredly say it was well worth the wait!<br />For the sake of clarity, I started with the first of the various series which make up the books set within the Realm of the Elderlings. This meant starting with Assassins Apprentice, the first installment in the Farseer Trilogy. <br />I have really fallen in love with Robin Hobb’s style of writing. It has so much substance and sophistication which I think high fantasies can sometimes miss. Having said that, she does not over complicate her writing, leaving more room for the plot to mature. I think she really excels in both her descriptions and her speech. When she describes the town, the court, even the hustle and bustle of where the trading ships dock, it is with such vibrancy and color that it carries through and inspires my own imagination. Likewise, Hobb has a very tight grip on the speech used within her works. Not once did I feel that there was a conversation which was stilted or unrealistic. I think this is also a tribute to her brilliant characterization, with the cast of characters all fully fledged beings in their own right.<br />One of the advantages of this novel was that whilst things were suggested, or links made, it was not necessarily obvious which thread was going to be fully followed. Even halfway through, I was still unsure which direction the novel could be heading. What also surprised me about this novel was that it was very self contained. There are definitely areas from which sequels and parallel series can spring, yet the book can also be read completely by itself. Most firsts in a series are quite slow, with the initial book used to set up and establish the rest in the series, but I did not find that here.<br /><br />One can expect so much from an author’s first novel, especially one titled after the two words that have become the salt and pepper of fantasy fiction through the decades. And yet, somehow, Robin Hobb takes these tropes that used to make fantasy great, and, with much confidence and palpable pleasure, creates such a captivating story that, when it is over, can result in a serious case of “book hangover”. This is what happens when characters in the hands of a talented author come to life and form a relationship with the reader. It is difficult to move forward to other stories and other worlds, much like saying goodbye to old friends. Thankfully, this is only the beginning of a long series that has set the bar high from the first book. This is the definition of great fantasy, a debut novel called Assassin’s Apprentice.<br /><br />My first foray into Robin Hobb’s world was a roaring success. It is so refreshing to find more women who are challenging the stereotypes of a genre which is so often favored by males. Assassin’s Apprentice was way better than anything I had expected. I wasn’t bored a second of it, even the courtly intrigues where interesting enough to keep my attention. Hobb writes with such naturalness that I could not help but be pulled in by the narrative she employs, and I cannot wait to delve further into the series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7660585558577680883" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1508730916" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1508730916" />
    <a title="Helen 2.0" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/39575951-helen-2-0"><img alt="Helen 2.0" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1460553725p2/39575951.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1508730916?book_show_action=true">Jul 21, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Helen 2.0" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Helen 2.0" href="/user/show/39575951-helen-2-0">Helen 2.0</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780006480099" href="/book/show/45107.Assassin_s_Apprentice">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39575951-helen-2-0?shelf=fantasy-epic">fantasy-epic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39575951-helen-2-0?shelf=brs-done">brs-done</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39575951-helen-2-0?shelf=royalty">royalty</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39575951-helen-2-0?shelf=rogues-thieves-assassins">rogues-thieves-assassins</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1508730916" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8376919357128991758"><blockquote>
  <i>Men cannot grieve as dogs do. But we grieve for many years.</i>
</blockquote><br/>Wow. This book really got under my skin. <br/><br/>At its core, <b>Assassin's Apprentice is a story about loneliness</b> - about a lonely boy, the bastard son of the former crown prince, growing up in a kingdom that does not want him. Fitz grows up among servants and soldiers in the king's palace, working in the shadow of his grandfather and uncles as a stableboy. Working with dogs, he discovers a talent for the Wit, a mental ability that allows him </span>
  <span id="freeText8376919357128991758" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>Men cannot grieve as dogs do. But we grieve for many years.</i>
</blockquote><br />Wow. This book really got under my skin. <br /><br />At its core, <b>Assassin's Apprentice is a story about loneliness</b> - about a lonely boy, the bastard son of the former crown prince, growing up in a kingdom that does not want him. Fitz grows up among servants and soldiers in the king's palace, working in the shadow of his grandfather and uncles as a stableboy. Working with dogs, he discovers a talent for the Wit, a mental ability that allows him to sense beings around him and forge emotional bonds with them. Eventually Fitz is recruited to train as a royal assassin for King Shrewd. <br /><br />The plot progression is slow, and certainly doesn't follow common plot structure guidelines. Robin Hobb takes her time describing the settings of each scene, as well as the nuances of each character and their standing to others in the book. As a result, <b>her fantasy world comes to life in gorgeous detail across the pages.</b> Descriptions of the kingdom and culture were vivid and will stay with me even if I do not continue this series.<br /><br />The author's writing also shines in the dialogue she creates; although Fitz is a quiet, reserved boy, he is often wrapped up in conversation by the servants and nobles of the castle. Every character's inner personality and motivations are subtly revealed in their speech, and <b>each line of dialogue is packed with meaning beyond the spoken words</b>. One of my favorite lines came from Fitz's mentor, Chade, speaking of becoming the king's man: <blockquote>
  <i>"It doesn't have to be that bad," Chade said quietly. "Most prisons are of our own making. A man makes his own freedom, too."</i>
</blockquote> Wise and moving dialogue like this was a dime a dozen in this book. <br /><br />So while the book was a slow read with little danger or excitement, I wouldn't have enjoyed it as much had Hobb cut some of the imagery and dialogue. <br /><br />I do have one complaint, which took one star off my rating. <b>Fitz, as a protagonist, is very passive</b>. Although he is often described by other characters, as well as the narrator, as a catalyst, Fitz generally does not drive the plot. Rather, the plot drives him. Much of the book features him reluctantly reacting to a problem at hand or observing the actions of others. That lack of initiative made it difficult to see how Fitz would become a legendary hero in later books. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8376919357128991758" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1904441963" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1904441963?book_show_action=true">Aug 21, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Warda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Warda" href="/user/show/30036082-warda">Warda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780007374038" href="/book/show/22012758-assassin-s-apprentice">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1904441963" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6906801400462896502">“Be your blood, boy, and ignore what anyone else thinks of you.”<br/><br/>I'm officially part of the Hobb fandom, hallelujah! This book was one of the most joyful slow-burners that I've read. Think 'The Name of the Wind.' It's about our precious Fitz, a bastard, who has been brought up by someone who used to work closely with his father. It is narrated by Fitz himself and we follow his life closely from childhood till his young teenage years. <br/><br/>The writing is quite simply, stunning. From page one I was hook</span>
  <span id="freeText6906801400462896502" style="display:none">“Be your blood, boy, and ignore what anyone else thinks of you.”<br /><br />I'm officially part of the Hobb fandom, hallelujah! This book was one of the most joyful slow-burners that I've read. Think 'The Name of the Wind.' It's about our precious Fitz, a bastard, who has been brought up by someone who used to work closely with his father. It is narrated by Fitz himself and we follow his life closely from childhood till his young teenage years. <br /><br />The writing is quite simply, stunning. From page one I was hooked on it. It's enchanting, immersive and has a dream-like feel to it. Hobb really has a way with story-telling. It lingers and stays with you. The style of narrative was just great. <br /><br />At times, it did feel a bit too slow for my personal taste. This is not the book to read if you're looking for a story that is fast-paced. The plot moves on its own accord, but there's so much to it! It really delves into Fitz's character, as well as others, and one really forms an attachment to him in particular. Seriously, Fitz had better be protected at all costs! My heart broke for him so many times whilst reading it! <br /><br />One random thing (not too random, since animals are key to the story) is that this book made me wish I had a dog. And I am not an animal person at all, but the way Hobb wrote the relationships our main character, who I almost feel like is my son now, had with dogs in this story just made me want to tear up constantly. It was so damn beautiful! <br /><br />I cannot wait to see how this story progresses. I'm SO excited to find out more about the magic system (Wit and Skill. One allows you to form this incredible, unique bond with animals and the other is like telephathy! SO COOL!!!), the world, and the Forged people. And of course, FITZ! 😍❤ </span>
  <a data-text-id="6906801400462896502" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1584305642" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1584305642" />
    <a title="Samir" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52081294-samir"><img alt="Samir" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588945560p2/52081294.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1584305642?book_show_action=true">Mar 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Samir" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Samir" href="/user/show/52081294-samir">Samir</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/25300963-assassin-s-apprentice">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1584305642" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2533749395504202466">Robin Hobb is an author which was on my radar for a long time and I was planning to read her books earlier but reading is a fickle and seductive mistress often taking us on an unplanned journeys and sometimes during those journeys we cross paths with people who manage to persuade us to follow their direction and just like that, I ended up in the Realms of the Elderlings, on a new adventure starting with the <i>Assassin’s Apprentice</i>. <br/><br/>This tale starts with our main character, Fitz (age 6), being brou</span>
  <span id="freeText2533749395504202466" style="display:none">Robin Hobb is an author which was on my radar for a long time and I was planning to read her books earlier but reading is a fickle and seductive mistress often taking us on an unplanned journeys and sometimes during those journeys we cross paths with people who manage to persuade us to follow their direction and just like that, I ended up in the Realms of the Elderlings, on a new adventure starting with the <i>Assassin’s Apprentice</i>. <br /><br />This tale starts with our main character, Fitz (age 6), being brought to the Farseer’s army outpost by his maternal grandfather and given to a soldier, who is told that he is King-in-Waiting Chivalry's bastard son. The soldier brings him to the commander of the outpost, Prince Verity, who orders that he be given into the care of Burrich, Chivalry's stablemaster and right-hand man. Before Burrich takes him to Buckkeep, the capital of the Six Duchies, his father abdicates from his position and retires to the Withywoods with his wife Patience so he never got the chance to meet him.<br /><br />Burrich is left with the task of raising him and being a stablemaster he teaches him how to take care of animals. During his time with animals he discovers he can bond telepathically with them and that is the form of magic called the Wit, an ancient magic which Burrich forbids him to practice. The Wit is very much similar to the Skill, a magic system practiced by the royal family, which gives them ability to share thoughts and strength. <br /><br />We follow the rest of story through a first person POV, so we pretty much see and feel the world and characters through the eyes and mind of our main protagonist thus creating a strong bond with him and that is something really important to me when reading; I need a character I can root for and Fitz is just that kind of character, not only did I root for him, he also managed to evoke a strong emotional empathy in me and that shows a great skill Hobb has in characterization.<br /><br />This is a slow paced book and I know that can be off putting for some readers who demand explosive action on every page because “nothing is happening” otherwise but in this case the pacing is suitable for the story because this is a character driven story with very strong emphasis on character development which was superbly done.<br /><br />The prose feels simple yet beautiful and often reminded me of Rothfuss’s writing and if I had to guess I would say that Hobb influenced him very much.<br /><br />I was completely mesmerized with the magic of this book. It is a beautiful coming-of-age tale which captivated my mind and made me realize why is it deemed a true classic and a pure fantasy gem.<br /><br />With the first quest completed, I’m ready for the next one and eager to find out what fate lies ahead for Fitz in the <i>Royal Assassin</i>. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2533749395504202466" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_143947269" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/143947269" />
    <a title="Kat" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4878104-kat"><img alt="Kat" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1515345527p2/4878104.jpg" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4878104-kat?shelf=blazing-intensity">blazing-intensity</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4878104-kat?shelf=political-intrigues">political-intrigues</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4878104-kat?shelf=robin-hobb">robin-hobb</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer143947269" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1244983022479907206">With the exciting news of a brand new series about Fitz & the Fool, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18658063-the-fool-s-assassin?from_search=true' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Fool's Assassin</a>, in mind, we are buddy reading this series in December and continue with the Tawny Man trilogy. <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1386518674i/7382307._SY540_.jpg' width='420' height='510' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Yup, I'm all set! (for some funky reason, I'd feel weird about reading Robin Hobb on my Kindle, so I got the entire series in English paperbacks too.:p<br/><br/>Buddy read with: <br/>*<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/4874641-kat' rel='nofollow noopener'>Kat</a> (joins for book 2) <br/>*<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/3481936-damian-dubois' rel='nofollow noopener'>Damian</a><br/>*<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/17225664-joshua' rel='nofollow noopener'>Joshua</a><br/>*<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/10017183-em' rel='nofollow noopener'>Em</a><br/>*<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/13173388-lee' rel='nofollow noopener'>Lee</a>(first timer, wooot!)<br/>*<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/3670048-erika' rel='nofollow noopener'>Erika</a>, and I'm confident we'll catch up with...<br/>*<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/3395391-daydreamer' rel='nofollow noopener'>DayDreamer</a> ;)<br/><br/>--------------------</span>
  <span id="freeText1244983022479907206" style="display:none">With the exciting news of a brand new series about Fitz &amp; the Fool, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18658063-the-fool-s-assassin?from_search=true" rel="nofollow noopener">The Fool's Assassin</a>, in mind, we are buddy reading this series in December and continue with the Tawny Man trilogy. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1386518674i/7382307._SY540_.jpg" width="420" height="510" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Yup, I'm all set! (for some funky reason, I'd feel weird about reading Robin Hobb on my Kindle, so I got the entire series in English paperbacks too.:p<br><br>Buddy read with: <br>*<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/4874641-kat" rel="nofollow noopener">Kat</a> (joins for book 2) <br>*<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/3481936-damian-dubois" rel="nofollow noopener">Damian</a><br>*<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/17225664-joshua" rel="nofollow noopener">Joshua</a><br>*<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/10017183-em" rel="nofollow noopener">Em</a><br>*<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/13173388-lee" rel="nofollow noopener">Lee</a>(first timer, wooot!)<br>*<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/3670048-erika" rel="nofollow noopener">Erika</a>, and I'm confident we'll catch up with...<br>*<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/3395391-daydreamer" rel="nofollow noopener">DayDreamer</a> ;)<br><br>------------------------------------------------------<br><b>Original review: January 2011</b><br>Boy, if I had never found this book in a discount shop as a teen... <br><br>A few Hobb trilogies further along the way, this is where it all started. At first <i>Assassin's Apprentice</i> seems like your typical fantasy book. Yep, the unwanted orphan, seaside fortress, clandestine politics, a good dash of magic and adventure are all present. However, Hobb is something else. <br><br>To say that these books are pretty intense is an understatement. I will just mention that while engrossed in the last chapters of the second book and then book three of this series, I actually started missing my train station. Twice. And had to wait for at least half an hour in the dark dreary February weather to catch a train the other way. Considering I usually don't enjoy being late for dinner and having to turn to crappy coffee in Styrofoam cups for comfort.. seriously, that SAYS something.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1244983022479907206" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1880226121" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1880226121" />
    <a title="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes"><img alt="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598297811p2/1452829.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1880226121?book_show_action=true">Jan 15, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" href="/user/show/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes">Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780006480099" href="/book/show/45107.Assassin_s_Apprentice">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes?shelf=year-2017">year-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes?shelf=3-star">3-star</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1880226121" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4223040974011115075"><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/77197.Assassin_s_Apprentice__Farseer_Trilogy___1_' title='Assassin's Apprentice (Farseer Trilogy, #1) by Robin Hobb' rel='nofollow noopener'>Assassin's Apprentice</a> is the story of Fitz, who arrives at Buckkeep barely more than a child. He is branded early on as the bastard of Prince Chivalry Farseer, eldest & deceased son of King Shrewd Farseer. And so begins the slow & steady descent of our main character into a life fraught with hardship after hardship.<br/><br/>Which brings us around to one of my main struggles with this story. The first 80-85% of this book is a slow trudge through Fitz's childhood, exploring the many brutal ways in which he</span>
  <span id="freeText4223040974011115075" style="display:none"><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/77197.Assassin_s_Apprentice__Farseer_Trilogy___1_" title="Assassin's Apprentice (Farseer Trilogy, #1) by Robin Hobb" rel="nofollow noopener">Assassin's Apprentice</a> is the story of Fitz, who arrives at Buckkeep barely more than a child. He is branded early on as the bastard of Prince Chivalry Farseer, eldest &amp; deceased son of King Shrewd Farseer. And so begins the slow &amp; steady descent of our main character into a life fraught with hardship after hardship.<br /><br />Which brings us around to one of my main struggles with this story. The first 80-85% of this book is a slow trudge through Fitz's childhood, exploring the many brutal ways in which he is ostracized by his peers, bullied by his superiors, &amp; deprived of the connections he so desperately desires. <br /><br /><b>Fitz's relentless misfortune definitely wore me out on an emotional level.</b><br /><br />It's not even that he's always suffering in some huge, dramatic way. Fitz's younger years are made up of a variety of large &amp; small hurts that, combined, would threaten to topple even a confident adult. I found this aspect of the story to be quite believable, <b>but exhausting.</b> <br /><br />There are definitely a lot of recognizable fantasy archetypes present here: <br /><br /><b>✘ Underdog/Bastard MC <br />✘ Gruff Father Figure<br />✘ Bratty Prince<br />✘ Wise Old Master<br />✘ Chosen One</b><br /><br />But I don't believe any one of them are written in a way that feels overdone. Each character is believable in their role &amp; defined enough that they transcend their archetypal labels. <br /><br />I would've liked to know a bit more about the world outside of Buckkeep. I have a decent idea about what goes on there, but not a very clear picture of the Duchies outside of that one or the surrounding lands. <br /><br />I think perhaps the strict first person PoV is a bit damaging in this respect because we are limited to experiencing places as Fitz visits them, and because he is a child for a lot of the book he spends most of his time at Buckkeep. But seeing that Hobb has shown herself to be a thorough writer, I feel as though this aspect will likely remedy itself in the later installments of the series. <br /><br />The two forms of magic introduced to us do help make up a bit of ground in the world building department. <b>The Wit &amp; The Skill</b> are both forms of mental connection, the former having to do with bonding to animals &amp; the latter having to do with subtly influencing the actions of people.<br /><br />I have heard for years that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/25307.Robin_Hobb" title="Robin Hobb" rel="nofollow noopener">Robin Hobb</a> is a queen among Fantasy authors, and purely from this first experience with her writing style I can definitely see why she has earned that reputation. Her way with words is <b>beautifully poised.</b> It's the kind of writing that falls into place so effortlessly that it inspires you to try your own hand at it. <br /><br />I found myself plenty of times thinking <i>"Wow what a lovely way to phrase that!"</i><br /><br />Speaking of writing, I think an important thing to know going into this series is that this first book is very <b>foundational.</b> It spends a lot of quality time developing Fitz through his adolescence, so much so that by the end you really do feel as though you've experienced years of his life. <br /><br />Because of this, the pace is absolutely slow. <b>Slow to the point that I was actually feeling the drag, and I typically don't have issues with a sluggish pace.</b> However, the climax of the book is certainly more exciting &amp; justifies all the time spent getting there. <br /><br />I don't know if I'll ever reread this book, as it is more of a framework than anything else. It is methodically crafted &amp; necessary, but to say I <b>enjoyed</b> it might give the wrong impression. I do <b>respect</b> it for what it is, and I believe it serves its purpose in setting the stage for events later to come.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4223040974011115075" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3184574478" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3184574478" />
    <a title="Hamad" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54464244-hamad"><img alt="Hamad" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577880699p2/54464244.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3184574478?book_show_action=true">Feb 10, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hamad" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hamad" href="/user/show/54464244-hamad">Hamad</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007562251" href="/book/show/21956219-assassin-s-apprentice">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54464244-hamad?shelf=paperbacks">paperbacks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54464244-hamad?shelf=adult-books">adult-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54464244-hamad?shelf=good-covers">good-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54464244-hamad?shelf=2020-reads">2020-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54464244-hamad?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3184574478" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12377492999180215399"><a href='https://thebookprescription.wordpress.com/2020/11/15/assassins-apprentice-review/' rel='nofollow noopener'>This Review</a> ✍️ <a href='https://thebookprescription.wordpress.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Blog</a> 📖 <a href='https://twitter.com/Hamad9626' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twitter</a> 🐦 <a href='https://www.instagram.com/thebookprescription/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Instagram</a> 📷<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“Nothing takes the heart out of a man more than the expectation of failure.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>I always wanted to read this series just because Hobb has one of the most humble GR bio and whenever I see it, I just think she is cool, I wanna read her books and the second reason is because adult fantasy is mostly written by men and a such a successful female author is not very common.<br/><br/>I also like to consider the setting the book was written in, this book was writt</span>
  <span id="freeText12377492999180215399" style="display:none"><a href="https://thebookprescription.wordpress.com/2020/11/15/assassins-apprentice-review/" rel="nofollow noopener">This Review</a> ✍️ <a href="https://thebookprescription.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> 📖 <a href="https://twitter.com/Hamad9626" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> 🐦 <a href="https://www.instagram.com/thebookprescription/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> 📷<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“Nothing takes the heart out of a man more than the expectation of failure.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>I always wanted to read this series just because Hobb has one of the most humble GR bio and whenever I see it, I just think she is cool, I wanna read her books and the second reason is because adult fantasy is mostly written by men and a such a successful female author is not very common.<br><br>I also like to consider the setting the book was written in, this book was written in 1995, that’s 25 effing years ago and it still is relevant to this day which is crazy! The author husband’s job and her hobbies include fishing, gardening, mushrooming and other stuff related to nature and it really shows in her writing. I guess what they say about writing what you know best is true after all!<br><br>The book follows the story of Fitz Farseer, he is the bastard son of Prince Chivalry, the story starts with his earliest memory as a six years old almost returned to the royal family, Chivalry who is the king-in-waiting decides to abdicate this post. Fitz gets blamed and then King Shrewd takes him under his wing and decides to teach and train him, that way he becomes one of the king’s men and he is trained under the king’s assassin as his apprentice.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“When you cut pieces out of the truth to avoid looking like a fool you end up looking like a moron instead.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>The book has both the extreme ratings of 1 and 5 stars, people tend to hate or love it, So how did I feel about this book? <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1605461820ra/30381875.gif" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It reminded me of observing snails as a kid, it is interesting to see these creatures walk slowly leaving a shiny trail behind them and then you would get fed up with the whole thing and you just want to spice things up and wish the snail could be faster (Not to spice it with salt though). These were more or less my feelings on this book. The book is very very sloooooow! One of the slowest most descriptive books I ever read. The writing is not bad which made me enjoy the beginning and I kept enjoying it until I got frustrated by not much happening specially past 50% of the book till the last 50 pages or so when the pace picks up again and things happen again.<br><br>The writing is good, I mean I once read that classics and older books were very descriptive and slow because people didn’t have access to internet like nowadays so authors had to describe everything. The problem is that things got much faster today and people prefer faster things and that explains why people gave this 1 star and couldn’t tolerate the writing. If you are a fan of slow reads then I don’t think you will have a problem with this. I should not that I specially liked the world’s folklore and history at the beginning of each chapter.<br><br>Fitz is a wholesome character, I think he has many upcoming books to grow in this series or the next books featuring him. I like what Hobb did when she named the characters as characteristics, I finally understood why! The characters didn’t stimulate much feelings from me but they weren’t bad. My favorite was The Fool because he was so odd and unique.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“Learning is never wrong. Even learning how to kill isn’t wrong. Or right. It’s just a thing to learn, a thing I can teach you. That’s all.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>The world-building is not very extensive, we get much descriptions but we don’t explore much of the world, the magic felt very basic and simple, it is just communicating with animals or between humans using a mental link. I wish we saw more of that to be honest.<br><br><b>Summary:</b> To be fair to the book, I understand both people who enjoyed it and those who did not, it takes great patience to got\ through one book and it is such a huge journey. The writing is good but overly-descriptive, the pace is very slow, the magic system is not complex but there is something wholesome about Fitz and the story that made me finish it. I think older me would have never been able to finish this. I will probably finish the trilogy and then decide what to do with the rest of the series!<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="12377492999180215399" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1290222128" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1290222128" />
    <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl"><img alt="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603085284p2/8734459.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1290222128?book_show_action=true">May 26, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl">Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=coming-of-age">coming-of-age</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1290222128" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9488867882394572127">After reading maybe a few too many YA fantasies, it was a breath of fresh air to delve into the world of Fitz, the assassin's apprentice. It was complex and layered, the way I like my fantasies and, I suppose, my reading generally (other than the brain-candy romance cravings, which tend to attack me randomly and without prior warning). <br/><br/>Fitz, the bastard son of the crown prince with a peasant woman, is taken from his mother as a six year old boy and dropped into the royal household. This novel fo</span>
  <span id="freeText9488867882394572127" style="display:none">After reading maybe a few too many YA fantasies, it was a breath of fresh air to delve into the world of Fitz, the assassin's apprentice. It was complex and layered, the way I like my fantasies and, I suppose, my reading generally (other than the brain-candy romance cravings, which tend to attack me randomly and without prior warning). <br /><br />Fitz, the bastard son of the crown prince with a peasant woman, is taken from his mother as a six year old boy and dropped into the royal household. This novel follows Fitz from his childhood, rejected by many and ignored by almost all others, to about age fifteen, as he grows in magical powers both with "the Wit," which allows him to share minds with animals, and "the Skill," a telepathic power. He also gains some more sinister learning, as the king's assassin, Chade, teaches him the skills of dealing out death to those that the king thinks need to be out of the way - for good reasons or bad. And the kingdom is under attack, both from within and without, so Fitz's peculiar skills will become necessary.<br /><br />There are mysteries and oddities about this world that are revealed slowly, but didn't give me the feeling that the author was hiding the ball just to stretch out the suspense. It's a book that made my brain work a little to follow all of the threads and layers, rather than making me want to skim ahead just to get to the end.<br /><br />Minus a star for being a little slow in parts and leaving several loose threads at the end. It's the first in a series, so I'm sure those threads get wrapped up later, but for the most part I think this works reasonably well as a stand-alone novel. Overall I thought it was a really intriguing fantasy, with enough depth and detail to really suck me into this world. I have to admit I haven't dashed off to read more books in this series, probably because reviews of later books indicate that it gets pretty dark, but I'm open to the idea.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9488867882394572127" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780006480099" href="/book/show/45107.Assassin_s_Apprentice">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/86504940-will-j-r-gwynne?shelf=favourite-series">favourite-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/86504940-will-j-r-gwynne?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/86504940-will-j-r-gwynne?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/86504940-will-j-r-gwynne?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2523652451" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12840137442187940553">My review of this AMAZING book is now on BookNest. <br/><br/><a href='https://booknest.eu/component/k2/william/1637-assassin-s-apprentice-farseer-trilogy-1-by-robin-hobb-book-review' rel='nofollow noopener'>Assassin's Apprentice BookNest</a><br/><br/><b>“Very little worth knowing is taught by fear.”</b><br/><br/>I read Assassin's Apprentice late last year, and how amazing it is that I did. This is the book that introduced me to my now second favourite author of all time. I blitzed through three trilogies in this world in less than a month! That is testament to how obsessed I became.<br/><br/>Hobb's characters are just a pure masterclass. Each has such a rare depth, and every action reveal</span>
  <span id="freeText12840137442187940553" style="display:none">My review of this AMAZING book is now on BookNest. <br /><br /><a href="https://booknest.eu/component/k2/william/1637-assassin-s-apprentice-farseer-trilogy-1-by-robin-hobb-book-review" rel="nofollow noopener">Assassin's Apprentice BookNest</a><br /><br /><b>“Very little worth knowing is taught by fear.”</b><br /><br />I read Assassin's Apprentice late last year, and how amazing it is that I did. This is the book that introduced me to my now second favourite author of all time. I blitzed through three trilogies in this world in less than a month! That is testament to how obsessed I became.<br /><br />Hobb's characters are just a pure masterclass. Each has such a rare depth, and every action reveals something about them, forming a vivid and real cast that deepened my love and connection in this book and the series. FitzChivalry Farseer is in my top 5 favourite fictional characters of all time, I think that explains my love.<br /><br /><b>“When you cut pieces out of the truth to avoid looking like a fool you end up looking like a moron instead.”</b><br /><br />The prose is more descriptive heavy than dialogue, but there is still a fair balance of speech. The interactions between characters are written fantastically and on the whole the prose is poetic and smooth and flawless. It is a literary genius in action.<br /><br />If you have not read this book, or any Hobb, I cannot stress enough that you should! It is a magnificent, wonderfully told story that will stay with me for many, many years, having become one of my top series of all time!<br /><br /><b>5/5 STARS</b></span>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('pXNV0McPEMUlHx0b/VdSBM08QVIPVuakT6RkpLdnb1pkPYWAiJd4me+4OUlj6gfE8lSo0mQqxzxHXXXx2/UdtA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('lymeF0n7uoKORQLFMULtQ29GaHbZxEOQIO8YX1WSMFZWZ05HBmPS3kTiJpev/7iDUC6B9rK4YggoFgkKOQBCuA==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer6588391329346411132">** I am shocked to find that some people think a 2 star 'I liked it' rating is a bad rating. What? I liked it. I LIKED it! That means I read the whole thing, to the last page, in spite of my life raining comets on me. It's a good book that survives the reading process with me. If a book is so-so, it ends up under the bed somewhere, or maybe under a stinky judo bag in the back of the van. So a 2 st</span>
  <span id="freeText6588391329346411132" style="display:none">** I am shocked to find that some people think a 2 star 'I liked it' rating is a bad rating. What? I liked it. I LIKED it! That means I read the whole thing, to the last page, in spite of my life raining comets on me. It's a good book that survives the reading process with me. If a book is so-so, it ends up under the bed somewhere, or maybe under a stinky judo bag in the back of the van. So a 2 star from me means,yes, I liked the book, and I'd loan it to a friend and it went everywhere in my jacket pocket or purse until I finished it. A 3 star means that I've ignored friends to finish it and my sink is full of dirty dishes. A 4 star means I'm probably in trouble with my editor for missing a deadline because I was reading this book. But I want you to know . . . I don't finish books I don't like. There's too many good ones out there waiting to be found.<br /><br /><br />Robin Hobb is the author of three well-received fantasy trilogies: The Farseer Trilogy (Assassin’s Apprentice, Royal Assassin, and Assassin’s Quest), The Liveship Traders Trilogy (Ship of Magic, Mad Ship and Ship of Destiny) and the Tawny Man Trilogy (Fool’s Errand, Golden Fool, and Fool’s Fate) Her current work in progress is entitled Shaman’s Crossing. Robin Hobb lives and works in Tacoma, Washington, and has been a professional writer for over 30 years.<br /><br />In addition to writing, her interests include gardening, mushrooming, and beachcombing. She and her husband Fred have three grown children and one teenager, and three grand-children.<br /><br />She also writes as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/53255.Megan_Lindholm" rel="nofollow noopener">Megan Lindholm</a>, and works under that name have been finalists for the Hugo award, the Nebula Award, and the Endeavor award. She has twice won an Isaac Asimov’s Science Fiction Readers’ Award.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6588391329346411132" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
